## IUK-T2-MAST251-006
**Block:** Mastery Exam (Kuphaldt)  
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** FAULT_ANALYSIS  
**Weight:** 2.0×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_mastery_textualized_IUK_MASTERY_INST251_x2_mastery_textualized  
**Format:** iuk_mastery_textualized  
**Review status:** ai_drafted_needs_sme_distractors  
**Textualized from diagram:** YES  

**Question:**  
[Diagram: A furnace temperature control loop diagram is provided, connecting a process area (Field Panel JB-12) to a control room panel (CP-1). The system includes the following components and connections:

**Process Area (Field Panel JB-12):**
*   **TE-205 (Thermocouple):** Type K, ungrounded tip, 0 to 1500 degrees Fahrenheit range. Its terminals A and B are connected to the input of TT-205.
*   **TT-205 (Temperature Transmitter):** Rosemount Model 444, 0 to 1500 degrees Fahrenheit input, 4-20 milliampere output. Its Red(+) output wire connects to TB-15 terminal 3. Its Black(-) output wire connects to TB-15 terminal 4.
*   **TY-205b (I/P Transducer):** Fisher Model 546, 4-20 milliampere input, 3-15 PSI output, coil resistance 176 ohm, fail-closed. Its Red(+) input connects to TB-15 terminal 5. Its Black(-) input connects to TB-15 terminal 6.
*   **TV-205 (Control Valve):** Fisher Easy-E, 3-15 PSI input, fail-closed. Receives a pneumatic signal from TY-205b and controls the 'Fuel to furnace'.

**Control Room Panel (CP-1):**
*   **Wiring for TT-205 signal:** Cable 3, Pair 1 connects TB-15 terminal 3 to TB-11 terminal 1 (Wht/Blu wire), and TB-15 terminal 4 to TB-11 terminal 2 (Blk wire).
*   **TIC-205 (Controller):** Siemens PAC 353, 1-5 Volt DC input, 0-1500 degrees Fahrenheit range, reverse-acting control. Its input terminals are labeled 1 (Red) and 2 (Blk).
*   **TY-205a (Resistor):** Vishay, 250 ohm. Connected in series on the positive input line to TIC-205. Specifically, the Wht/Blu wire from TB-11 terminal 1 connects to one side of TY-205a, and the other side of TY-205a connects to TIC-205 terminal 1 (Red). The Blk wire from TB-11 terminal 2 connects directly to TIC-205 terminal 2 (Blk).
*   **Loop Power Supply:** A 24 VDC power source is indicated, with its positive terminal connected to TB-11 terminal 7 (Red wire). This 24 VDC supplies the 4-20 milliampere current loop that includes TT-205, TY-205a, and the input of TIC-205.
*   **Wiring for TIC-205 output:** TIC-205 output terminals 20 (Red) and 21 (Blk) connect to TB-11 terminals 17 (Red) and 18 (Blk) respectively. These signals then connect from TB-11 terminals 17 (Red) to TB-11 terminal 8 (Wht/Org), and from TB-11 terminal 18 (Blk) to TB-11 terminal 9 (Org). These connect via Cable 3, Pair 2 to TB-15 terminals 5 (Red) and 6 (Blk) for TY-205b's input.
*   **Main Power:** An ES 120 VAC Breaker #4 at Panel L2 is indicated as providing main electrical power for the control panel components.

**Observed Symptoms:**
*   The Indicating Controller (TIC-205) displays a furnace temperature of -375 degrees Fahrenheit.
*   A voltmeter connected between terminals 1 and 2 of the TIC-205 (the controller's input terminals) registers 24 VDC.

Identify the likelihood of each specified fault for this circuit. Consider each fault one at a time (i.e., no coincidental faults), determining whether or not each fault could independently account for all measurements and symptoms in this circuit. For each fault, state whether it is 'Possible' or 'Impossible' and provide a brief justification.

**Faults to evaluate:**
1.  TY-205a failed open.
2.  TY-205b electrically failed open (output low).
3.  TT-205 failed open.
4.  Wire open between terminal 6 and terminal 9 (referring to TB-15 terminal 6 and TB-11 terminal 9).
5.  Wire open between terminal 1 and terminal 7 (referring to TB-11 terminal 1 and TB-11 terminal 7).
6.  Valve #15 at column #8 shut off (referring to TV-205).
7.  Breaker #4 at panel L2 tripped (off).

**Correct Answer:**  
1.  **TY-205a failed open:** **Possible.** If the 250 ohm resistor TY-205a fails open, the 4-20 milliampere current loop supplying the TIC-205 input becomes an open circuit. This would cause the current to drop to 0 milliamperes, resulting in 0 volts across the resistor. The TIC-205 would interpret this 0-volt input as the lowest possible temperature, consistent with -375 degrees Fahrenheit. A voltmeter placed across the open resistor (TIC-205 terminals 1 and 2), with the 24 VDC loop power supply still active and attempting to drive current through the open loop, would measure the full 24 VDC open-circuit voltage.
2.  **TY-205b electrically failed open (output low):** **Impossible.** TY-205b is an I/P transducer located in the output control loop (from TIC-205 to TV-205). A failure in this component would affect the control valve's position but would not directly impact the temperature measurement input loop (TE-205 -> TT-205 -> TIC-205 input). Therefore, it cannot explain the -375 degrees Fahrenheit reading or the 24 VDC at the TIC-205 input terminals.
3.  **TT-205 failed open:** **Possible.** If the temperature transmitter TT-205 fails open, its 4-20 milliampere output current loop becomes an open circuit. This would cause the current to drop to 0 milliamperes, resulting in 0 volts at the TIC-205 input. The TIC-205 would interpret this 0-volt input as the lowest possible temperature, consistent with -375 degrees Fahrenheit. With the current loop open and the 24 VDC loop power supply still active, a voltmeter across the TIC-205 input terminals 1 and 2 (which are across TY-205a) would measure the full 24 VDC open-circuit voltage.
4.  **Wire open between terminal 6 and terminal 9 (TB-15 terminal 6 and TB-11 terminal 9):** **Impossible.** This wire connects the negative side of the TIC-205's output loop to the input of TY-205b (specifically, TB-15 terminal 6 and TB-11 terminal 9 are connected via Cable 3, Pair 2). An open circuit here would affect the operation of the I/P transducer and the control valve but would not impact the temperature measurement input loop to TIC-205. Therefore, it cannot explain the -375 degrees Fahrenheit reading or the 24 VDC at the TIC-205 input terminals.
5.  **Wire open between terminal 1 and terminal 7 (TB-11 terminal 1 and TB-11 terminal 7):** **Possible.** TB-11 terminal 7 is connected to the 24 VDC loop power supply. TB-11 terminal 1 is part of the positive signal path from the TT-205 to the TIC-205 input (via TY-205a). An open wire anywhere in the primary 4-20 milliampere current loop (which includes the 24 VDC supply, TT-205, and the TIC-205 input circuitry including TY-205a) would result in 0 milliamperes of current. This leads to 0 volts at the TIC-205 input, which is interpreted as -375 degrees Fahrenheit. With the loop open and the 24 VDC loop power supply still active, a voltmeter across the TIC-205 input terminals 1 and 2 (across TY-205a) would measure the full 24 VDC open-circuit voltage.
6.  **Valve #15 at column #8 shut off (TV-205):** **Impossible.** TV-205 is the final control element, a mechanical valve. While a stuck-closed valve would prevent fuel from entering the furnace and cause the furnace temperature to drop, it is a mechanical issue that would not directly cause an electrical open circuit in the temperature measurement loop. It cannot explain the 24 VDC measured at the TIC-205 input terminals.
7.  **Breaker #4 at panel L2 tripped (off):** **Impossible.** Breaker #4 provides 120 VAC main power to the control panel, which is assumed to supply the 24 VDC loop power for the instrumentation. If this breaker trips, the 24 VDC loop power supply would also be off. While a loss of loop power would result in 0 milliamperes current and a -375 degrees Fahrenheit reading by the TIC-205, the voltmeter across the TIC-205 input terminals (1 and 2) would then read 0 VDC, not 24 VDC, because the power source itself is off.

**Required Elements:**
- [DRAFT — SME to specify]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Scoring Rubric:**
| Score | Criteria |
|-------|----------|
| Full | 10/10 — all 1 required elements present and accurate |
| Partial (high) | 7/10 — most elements correct |
| Partial (low) | 4/10 — partial answer, key element missing |
| Zero | 0/10 — incorrect or missing core concept |

**Reference:** Kuphaldt INST mastery

**Difficulty Rationale:** Requires understanding of 4-20mA current loops, voltage drops across series resistors, interpretation of open-circuit conditions with a voltmeter, controller behavior (reverse-acting, interpreting low/fault input), and tracing signal paths through a moderately complex industrial control diagram to determine root causes of observed symptoms.

Describe the function of each component of a HART signal: the 4–20 mA analog signal, the FSK (Frequency Shift Keying) digital overlay, the HART physical layer requirements, and what a multidrop configuration is and when it would be used.

**Correct Answer:**

## IUK-T2-PROC-016
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe the procedure for transferring a PID controller from AUTO to MANUAL mode without causing a process bump, and then describe how to transfer back from MANUAL to AUTO mode bump-free.

**Correct Answer:**  
**AUTO to MANUAL (bump-free):**
A "bump" occurs if the manual output value differs from the current controller output at the moment of transfer.

Bump-free transfer AUTO → MANUAL:
1. Observe the current controller output value (e.g., 45%)
2. Set the manual output to exactly match the current controller output (45%) BEFORE switching modes
3. Switch to MANUAL — since the manual output matches the auto output exactly, no change occurs in the valve
4. Now the operator can manually adjust the output as needed

Most modern DCS systems implement "bumpless transfer" automatically — when switching to MANUAL, the manual output is pre-loaded with the current auto output. Verify your DCS does this; older systems may require manual matching.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Scoring Rubric:**
Full credit = both directions with output matching described. One direction only = 50%.

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.29; ISA-5.9

## IUK-T2-PROC-018
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC

**Adversarial:** NO

**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe the complete procedure for calibrating a 4–20 mA pressure transmitter (0–300 PSI range) using a deadweight tester as the pressure reference. Include preparation, procedure steps, and acceptance criteria.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Preparation:**
1. Review the transmitter datasheet and calibration sheet — confirm model, serial number, range, accuracy spec
2. Verify deadweight tester calibration is current (traceable certificate, within calibration interval)
3. Ensure deadweight tester is rated for the pressure range
4. Gather calibrated milliamp reference meter (4.5-digit minimum)
5. Confirm process isolation is complete — transmitter is isolated and depressurized
6. Allow transmitter and deadweight tester to reach thermal equilibrium (especially important at extremes of temperature)

## IUK-T2-PROC-020
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
You need to perform a HART command to trim the sensor zero on a pressure transmitter currently reading 0.12 PSI with no pressure applied. Describe the complete HART trim procedure using a HART Field Communicator, including what commands to use and what precautions to take.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Pre-trim precautions:**
1. Confirm the transmitter is at true zero pressure — process is isolated, equalizing valve is open, impulse line is vented to atmosphere. The reading of 0.12 PSI must be confirmed as a true zero error, not a residual process pressure.
2. Allow sufficient time for the transmitter to stabilize at zero (typically 5 minutes after isolation and venting)
3. Document the current as-found condition

## IUK-T2-PROC-022
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe the complete procedure for performing a partial stroke test (PST) on an on/off safety valve using a smart digital valve controller (DVC). Include what is being tested, the pass/fail criteria, and any process considerations.

**Correct Answer:**  
**What is being tested:**
A partial stroke test verifies that an on/off safety valve (typically a SIS final element) can actually move from its normal position when commanded — proving that it is not seized, corroded, stuck, or mechanically frozen. It does this without fully stroking the valve, minimizing process impact.

**Question:**  
Describe what a "process loop check" is (not a calibration — a loop check), the sequence of steps, what constitutes a pass, and why it is performed separately from calibration.

**Correct Answer:**  
**What a loop check is:**
A loop check verifies that the complete instrument loop — from field sensor through all wiring, marshalling, DCS I/O card, configuration, and operator display — functions correctly as an integrated system. It is distinct from calibration, which verifies the accuracy of the measurement device alone.

## IUK-T2-PROC-026
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC

**Question:**  
Explain the procedure for verifying and setting the "analog output trim" on a HART transmitter. When is this needed, and how does it differ from "sensor trim"?

**Correct Answer:**  
**What is analog output trim:**
Analog output trim corrects the digital-to-analog (D/A) conversion — the final step where the transmitter converts its calculated process value into a 4–20 mA output current. Even if the transmitter's internal measurement is correct, the D/A conversion can have small offset or gain errors causing the mA output to differ slightly from the ideal value.

## IUK-T2-PROC-029
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Explain the Ziegler-Nichols closed-loop (ultimate gain) tuning method: what is the procedure, what are the ultimate gain (Ku) and ultimate period (Tu), and what are the resulting PID tuning equations?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Procedure:**
1. Set the controller to proportional-only (set I to off/maximum reset time, D to off/zero)
2. Put the controller in AUTO
3. Slowly increase the proportional gain (decrease proportional band) until the process variable begins to oscillate continuously with a constant, stable amplitude — sustained oscillation, neither growing nor dying
4. The gain at this point is the **Ultimate Gain (Ku)**
5. Measure the **Ultimate Period (Tu)** — the period of the sustained oscillation in minutes

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Scoring Rubric:**
Full credit = procedure, Ku/Tu definition, all three tuning tables, and at least one limitation. Missing limitations = 75%.

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.29; Ziegler-Nichols (1942) original paper

---

## IUK-T2-PROC-034
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What is the correct procedure for commissioning a new 4–20 mA analog input channel on a DCS, from the physical I/O card level through to the operator display? List all steps in order.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Complete commissioning sequence:**

1. **Hardware verification:**
   - Confirm I/O card type matches the signal type (AI 4-20mA card, not DI or other)
   - Verify card is installed in correct slot per I/O schedule
   - Confirm 24V loop supply is present (check DCS loop supply power)

2. **Physical wiring check:**
   - Verify field wiring terminations at marshalling panel match the loop drawing (correct channel, correct polarity, shielding grounded at one end)
   - Confirm cable continuity if field device is not yet installed

3. **I/O card configuration (DCS I/O level):**
   - Configure channel as 4-20mA input in DCS I/O configuration tool
   - Set input range (4-20mA)
   - Assign physical channel to its logical I/O tag

4. **Controller/software configuration:**
   - Link the physical I/O channel to the correct controller AI (analog input) function block
   - Configure the engineering unit scaling (e.g., 4mA=0 GPM, 20mA=500 GPM)
   - Set engineering unit label
   - Configure alarm setpoints (high, low, high-high, low-low)
   - Configure bad PV actions (fault low, fault high behavior on signal loss)

5. **Signal simulation (loop check):**
   - Inject 4mA, 12mA, 20mA at the field terminal using a precision current source
   - Verify DCS faceplate displays 0%, 50%, 100% (or correct engineering unit values)
   - Verify alarm activations at correct engineering unit values
   - Verify signal loss detection (disconnect loop — DCS should indicate fault)

6. **Field device connection and verification:**
   - Connect actual transmitter; verify live reading
   - Confirm reading is reasonable for current process conditions

7. **Documentation:**
   - Record channel number, tag number, scaling, alarm setpoints, verification results
   - Update as-built documentation if any discrepancies found

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Scoring Rubric:**
Full credit = all 7 phases in order. 5+ phases = 80%. Signal simulation step specifically included = required for full credit.

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.4; DCS supplier commissioning documentation

## IUK-T2-PROC-037
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe the procedure for manually tuning a PID controller using the "trial and error" method for a temperature loop with known sluggish response characteristics (large thermal mass, long time constant).

**Correct Answer:**  
**Characteristics of a sluggish process (temperature, large thermal mass):**
- Long time constant — PV responds slowly to output changes
- May have significant dead time before any PV response begins
- Low process gain (large output change required for small PV change)
- Tends toward sluggish correction, not oscillation
- Integral (reset) tends to be needed; derivative often useful

**Question:**  
What is a "functional safety assessment" (FSA) as defined in IEC 61511, when must it be performed, and who should conduct it?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Functional Safety Assessment (FSA):**
A structured, documented review and audit of a SIS design and implementation to verify that all functional safety requirements have been correctly identified, allocated, and realized in the actual installed system. It is not a design review — it assesses whether the installed system actually achieves the required functional safety.

## IUK-T2-PROC-046
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe what "loop impedance testing" is, when it is performed for an IS (intrinsically safe) circuit, and what the pass criteria are.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Loop impedance testing for IS circuits:**
In intrinsically safe systems, safety depends on limiting the energy that can enter the hazardous area to levels below ignition thresholds. The IS barrier (Zener or galvanic) has defined maximum output parameters (Voc, Isc, Ca, La). The field wiring and device connected to the barrier must have capacitance and inductance values that, when combined with the circuit's stored energy, remain below the barrier's allowed entity parameters.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Scoring Rubric:**
Full credit = what is tested + three test types + when performed + pass criteria.

**Reference:** IEC 60079-14 (Electrical installations in hazardous areas); ISA RP12.6; IEC 60079-25

Describe what a Factory Acceptance Test (FAT) for a SIS logic solver is, what it should verify, and how it differs from a Site Acceptance Test (SAT).

**Correct Answer:**  
**Factory Acceptance Test (FAT):**
A formal, documented test of the SIS logic solver (safety PLC, relay system, or hardwired interlock panel) performed at the manufacturer's facility before delivery to site. It verifies that the programmed logic, I/O assignments, communication, and hardware configuration comply with the Safety Requirements Specification (SRS) and SIS design documentation.

## IUK-T2-PROC-087
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe the correct procedure for zeroing a differential pressure transmitter using a 3-valve manifold after installation in liquid service with the transmitter mounted BELOW the process taps.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Standard 3-valve manifold equalization and zero procedure:**

1. **Ensure both isolation valves (HP and LP) are CLOSED** and the equalizer valve is CLOSED. Transmitter is isolated.

2. **Slowly open the EQUALIZER valve** — this connects HP and LP sides of the transmitter to each other, creating equal pressure on both sides. The transmitter should now read approximately zero DP.

3. **Slowly open the HP isolation valve** — process pressure now applies equally to both sides (through the equalizer). Transmitter remains at equal pressure.

4. **Slowly open the LP isolation valve** — both sides now see process pressure through manifold pathways.

5. **Close the equalizer valve** — the transmitter is now in full differential service. Allow impulse lines to stabilize (purge air if needed).

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.7; 3-valve manifold standard operating procedure

---

## IUK-T2-PROC-093
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
A technician must replace a thermocouple in a thermowell on a live process pipe. The process is at 300°F and 150 PSIG. Describe the safe procedure for replacement.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Safe hot-swap procedure for thermocouple in thermowell:**

1. **Verify process conditions:** Confirm the operating temperature (300°F) and pressure (150 PSIG) are within the thermowell's rated conditions and that removal of the thermocouple head leaves the thermowell sealed (the well itself, not the thermocouple, provides the pressure seal).

2. **Hot work permit (if required):** For temperatures above 150°F or any pressurized system, a hot work or hot tap permit may be required per site procedures. Obtain applicable permits.

3. **PPE:** Wear appropriate PPE — heat-resistant gloves, face shield (for steam/fluid splash risk at 300°F), appropriate hearing protection if needed. DO NOT use bare hands on the thermowell housing.

4. **Inform the control room:** Notify the process operator that the temperature indication (TI/TT) for this location will be lost during replacement. If the instrument is used in control or safety function, place in manual/bypass per procedure.

5. **Disconnect electrical:** De-energize and disconnect the thermocouple extension leads from the transmitter head. Lock and tag the circuit if required.

6. **Remove the thermocouple:** Unscrew the thermocouple from the thermowell. The thermowell remains installed in the pipe — only the measuring element is removed. There should be NO process fluid release (thermowell is sealed into the pipe independently).

7. **Inspect the thermowell:** While the thermocouple is out, inspect the thermowell bore for corrosion, plugging, or damage. Look for any process leakage from the well connection.

8. **Install new thermocouple:** Insert the new thermocouple of the correct type (match the original: J, K, etc.) and length (must match thermowell immersion depth) into the thermowell. Tighten per spec (typically snug + 1/4 turn for compression-type fittings, or thread engagement per standard).

9. **Reconnect electrical:** Connect extension wires with correct polarity (thermocouple leads are polarized — positive and negative must match). Verify thermocouple type matches the transmitter configuration.

10. **Verify reading:** Confirm the temperature reading is reasonable for current process conditions. Note: new thermocouple may take minutes to reach thermal equilibrium in the thermowell.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.9; thermocouple installation best practices; OSHA hot work requirements

**Question:**  
Describe the HART Communication protocol's physical layer and explain how a HART signal can coexist on the same wire pair as a 4–20 mA analog signal.

**Correct Answer:**  
**HART Physical Layer:**
HART (Highway Addressable Remote Transducer) uses the Bell 202 frequency-shift keying (FSK) standard for its physical layer. It superimposes a digital signal on top of the 4–20 mA analog current loop.

## IUK-T2-PROC-107
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What is LOTO (Lockout/Tagout) and when is it required for instrument work? Give two specific examples of when LOTO applies and one example where it does NOT apply.

**Correct Answer:**  
**LOTO (Lockout/Tagout):**
LOTO is a safety procedure required by OSHA 29 CFR 1910.147 (Control of Hazardous Energy) that physically prevents energy sources from being re-energized during maintenance or servicing activities. Workers apply personal padlocks (lockout) or tags (tagout) to energy isolation points — electrical breakers, valve handles, pneumatic supply — to ensure the equipment cannot be operated while someone is working on it.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** OSHA 29 CFR 1910.147; Kuphaldt LIII Ch.2; site LOTO procedures

**Question:**  
Describe the correct procedure for performing a "zero trim" on a HART-enabled differential pressure transmitter that reads 0.15 inH₂O when both impulse lines are equalized (actual DP = 0). Include the conditions that must be met before performing the trim.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Pre-conditions:**
1. Both block valves CLOSED (or process isolated)
2. Equalizing valve OPEN (both sides of the transmitter see identical pressure)
3. Allow time for pressures to equalize (minimum 30 seconds; longer for gas service)
4. Confirm the transmitter is in normal operating mode (not in alarm/diagnostic)

## IUK-T2-PROC-140
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
A technician needs to replace a control valve positioner in the field while the process is running. The valve is air-to-open, spring-return, and currently controlling at ~50% open. Describe the correct procedure to safely swap the positioner without causing a process upset.

**Correct Answer:**  
1. **Notify the control room operator** — inform them you will be working on the valve and it may move during the swap
2. **Place the controller in MANUAL** at the control room — this freezes the output and prevents the controller from reacting to process changes during the work
3. **Record the current controller output** (e.g., 50%) and the current air pressure to the actuator
4. **If available, install a bypass (hand jack or manual override)** to hold the valve at current position mechanically
5. **Slowly bleed the output air to the positioner** — if the valve is ATO/spring-return, it will fail CLOSED. If this is unacceptable, use the manual override or temporary air supply to hold position
6. **Disconnect and remove the old positioner**
7. **Mount the new positioner** with correct linkage/feedback connection
8. **Restore air supply** and verify the valve moves to approximately the commanded position
9. **Calibrate the new positioner** (zero and span) against the 4–20 mA or 3–15 PSI input
10. **Transfer back to AUTO** and monitor the process for proper control

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.26; site-specific MOC procedures

---

## IUK-T2-PROC-151
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
A control valve is oscillating rapidly (cycling) while the process variable is stable. The loop is in automatic. List three possible causes and the first diagnostic step for each.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Cause 1: Valve stiction (static friction)**
- The valve sticks, then breaks free with a jump, then sticks again — causing limit-cycle oscillation
- **Diagnostic:** Put controller in MANUAL and slowly ramp the output — observe if the valve position jumps in discrete steps instead of moving smoothly

- [not specified in source]

- [DRAFT — SME review required]

## IUK-T2-PROC-153
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×

**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe the correct procedure for performing a "bump test" on a control loop to evaluate the process response. What information does this test provide for PID tuning?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Procedure:**
1. Place the controller in MANUAL mode with the process at steady state
2. Record the current PV and CO values
3. Make a step change in the controller output (typically 5–10% of output range)
4. Record the PV response over time — capture the full response until PV reaches a new steady state
5. Plot PV vs. time to characterize the process dynamics

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.28

## IUK-T2-PROC-157
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
An operator reports a level transmitter reading "frozen" at 47%. The actual level is changing (verified by sight glass). The transmitter is 4–20 mA, HART-enabled. List the systematic troubleshooting steps to isolate the fault.

**Correct Answer:**  
1. **Check the DCS/PLC side first:**
   - Is the AI card reading the correct mA? (Check raw mA value in DCS diagnostics)
   - If DCS shows a changing mA value but the display is frozen → display/software/bad-quality tag issue, not a field problem

2. **Measure loop current at the DCS AI terminals:**
   - If current is stuck at a fixed value (e.g., 10.72 mA = 47%) → field-side issue
   - If current is varying normally → DCS input fault

3. **Measure loop current at the transmitter terminals:**
   - If transmitter output is fixed → transmitter fault or frozen measurement
   - If transmitter output is varying → wiring issue between transmitter and DCS (intermittent short, ground fault, terminal corrosion)

4. **If transmitter output is frozen — connect HART communicator:**
   - Read the primary variable (PV) — is the internal sensor reading changing?
   - If PV is changing but output is frozen → transmitter output circuitry failure
   - If PV is also frozen → sensor failure or blocked impulse lines

5. **Check impulse lines / process connections:**
   - Plugged impulse lines (most common cause of "frozen" level readings)
   - Frozen condensate in lines (cold weather)
   - Closed isolation valve

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.4, Ch.11

---

## IUK-T2-PROC-159
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What is the correct procedure for performing a "LOTO" (Lock Out / Tag Out) on a 4–20 mA instrument loop powered by a 24 VDC supply in the marshaling cabinet? Include the specific energy isolation points.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Procedure per OSHA 29 CFR 1910.147:**

1. **Notify affected personnel** — operators, control room, maintenance coordinator
2. **Identify all energy sources:** 24 VDC power supply in the marshaling cabinet (primary), any pneumatic supply to valve positioner (secondary), any associated process isolation
3. **De-energize the circuit:**
   - Remove the fuse or switch off the breaker feeding the 24 VDC supply to this loop
   - OR: Disconnect the wires at the power supply terminal strip
4. **Lock out the energy isolation point:**
   - Apply a personal padlock to the fuse block, breaker, or disconnect switch
   - If no lockable disconnect exists, use a lock box on the removed fuse
5. **Tag out:** Attach a DANGER tag with your name, date, reason, and contact information
6. **Verify zero energy:**
   - Measure voltage at the field terminals with a multimeter — confirm 0 VDC
   - Attempt to read the loop on the DCS — confirm BAD/OFFLINE status
7. **If pneumatic energy exists:** Bleed the air supply to any valve actuator and lock/tag the air isolation valve

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** OSHA 29 CFR 1910.147; Kuphaldt LIII Ch.20

---

## IUK-T2-PROC-161
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
A new pressure transmitter has been installed in the field but the DCS shows a constant 3.6 mA. Per NAMUR NE 43, what does 3.6 mA indicate, and what are the three most common commissioning errors that cause this?

**Correct Answer:**  
Per NAMUR NE 43: **3.6 mA = sensor/electronics failure indication (low-side fault signal).** The transmitter is deliberately driving its output below 4 mA to signal that it has detected an internal fault.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

## IUK-T2-PROC-165
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
An operator wants to switch a cascade control loop from CASCADE to LOCAL setpoint. Describe the correct transfer procedure and what could go wrong if done improperly.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Correct procedure:**
1. Place the SECONDARY controller in LOCAL setpoint mode (this disconnects the primary controller's output from the secondary's setpoint)
2. The secondary controller now holds its current setpoint — the output should not change (bumpless transfer)
3. If desired, the operator can then adjust the secondary setpoint manually

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.28

## IUK-T2-PROC-167
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe the correct procedure for installing an RTD in a thermowell, including the critical steps that affect measurement accuracy.

**Correct Answer:**  
1. **Verify thermowell compatibility:** Confirm the RTD probe length matches the thermowell bore depth (the sensor tip must reach the bottom of the thermowell)
2. **Inspect the thermowell bore:** Ensure it is clean, dry, free of corrosion or debris
3. **Apply thermal compound:** Fill the thermowell bore with a heat-transfer compound (thermal grease or conductive oil) to eliminate the air gap between the RTD sheath and the thermowell bore. **This is the #1 accuracy-critical step** — an air gap significantly increases thermal lag and reduces accuracy.
4. **Insert the RTD probe:** Slide it gently to the bottom of the thermowell without forcing
5. **Connect the wiring:** Follow the 2/3/4-wire connection diagram on the transmitter, ensuring the correct lead identification (for 3-wire: the two same-color leads go to the compensation terminals)
6. **Secure the connection head:** Tighten the compression fitting or thread to seal against moisture
7. **Verify reading:** Compare the initial reading against a known process condition or portable reference thermometer

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.10

## IUK-T2-PROC-172
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC

**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
A field technician finds that a control valve positioner indicates 50% travel, but the valve stem indicator shows approximately 35%. What are three possible causes, and what is the correct resolution for each?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Cause 1: Feedback linkage misalignment**
The feedback arm connecting the valve stem to the positioner is bent, loose, or incorrectly positioned. The positioner "thinks" the valve is at 50% because its feedback says so, but the actual position is different.

A facility uses FOUNDATION Fieldbus (FF) for a reactor temperature control loop. The transmitter, controller, and valve positioner are all FF devices on the same H1 segment. Where does the PID control execute — in the DCS, in the transmitter, or in the positioner? Explain why.

**Correct Answer:**  
In a FOUNDATION Fieldbus system, the PID control function block typically executes **in the field device** — most commonly in the **transmitter** or in the **positioner/valve controller**, not in the DCS.

## IUK-T2-PROC-179
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
An instrument technician is tasked with calibrating a safety relief valve (SRV) on a pressure vessel. What specific steps must be taken BEFORE and AFTER the calibration, beyond the normal calibration procedure?

**Correct Answer:**  
**BEFORE calibration:**
1. **Verify Management of Change (MOC) if applicable:** If the SRV set pressure is being changed, an MOC must be completed and approved
2. **Confirm the vessel is properly protected during SRV removal:** Either a spare SRV is in place (dual SRV installation with changeover valve), or the vessel is depressured and isolated, or a temporary exemption with compensating measures is documented
3. **Review the vessel nameplate/data report** for MAWP and confirm the SRV set pressure matches design requirements
4. **Tag the SRV** with its unique identification and vessel it protects

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** ASME Section VIII; API 576; OSHA PSM 29 CFR 1910.119

## IUK-T2-PROC-181
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
A control room operator observes that a temperature PID controller output is "railed" at 100% but the PV is still 10°F below setpoint. What are the four most likely causes?

**Correct Answer:**  
1. **Undersized final element:** The control valve is too small (insufficient Cv) to deliver enough heat input at current process conditions. The controller asks for maximum output, but the valve at 100% still can't provide enough energy.

2. **Process demand exceeds design:** The heat load has increased beyond design capacity (e.g., higher throughput, colder feed temperature, additional heat losses). The heating system simply cannot keep up.

3. **Final element failure:** The control valve is stuck, air supply is lost, positioner has failed, or the valve is fully open but something is blocking flow through it (plugged strainer, tripped pump).

4. **Heat source problem:** If the heating medium is steam — steam pressure may be low (supply header pressure drop, PRV station issue). If electric — heater element has failed, SCR has failed, or a fuse is blown.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.28

---

**3-valve manifold:** Contains HP block valve, LP block valve, and equalizing valve. Standard for most DP transmitter installations. Adequate for non-hazardous and moderate-pressure applications.

## IUK-T2-PROC-197
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What are the three standard methods for mounting an orifice plate in a pipeline, and what determines which method is used?

**Correct Answer:**  
1. **Orifice flange union (paddle-type):** The orifice plate is sandwiched between two special flanges with built-in pressure taps. Most common in North America. Easy to inspect and replace the plate.

2. **Orifice fitting (senior/junior fitting):** A permanent fitting welded to the pipe that allows the orifice plate to be inserted and removed without breaking the flanged joint — some designs allow plate replacement under pressure (slide-type). Used in high-maintenance or frequently-inspected applications.

3. **Integral orifice:** The orifice is built into the transmitter body or a small manifold. Used for small lines (typically ≤2") and low flow rates.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.12

## IUK-T2-PROC-199
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
A technician needs to configure a HART transmitter for the first time using a handheld communicator. List the minimum configuration parameters that must be set and their significance.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Minimum configuration parameters:**

1. **Tag:** Unique ISA-5.1 identifier (e.g., FT-201). Identifies the device in the system. Must match the loop diagram and DCS tag.

2. **Lower Range Value (LRV):** The process value that corresponds to 4 mA. Must match the DCS scaling.

3. **Upper Range Value (URV):** The process value that corresponds to 20 mA. Must match the DCS scaling.

4. **Engineering units:** The units for the primary variable (PSI, inH₂O, °F, GPM, etc.). Must match the DCS display.

5. **Transfer function:** Linear or square root. For flow applications, determines whether square root extraction is performed in the transmitter or must be done in the DCS.

6. **Damping:** Time constant for output smoothing (typically 0.2–2.0 seconds). Affects response speed vs. noise filtering.

7. **Sensor type (if applicable):** For temperature transmitters: RTD type (PT100, PT1000) or thermocouple type (J, K, T, etc.)

8. **Fail mode:** Output on sensor failure — upscale (21 mA), downscale (3.6 mA), or last value. Must match the safety philosophy.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.4; HART Field Device Specification

---

**Question:**  
What is the correct procedure for blowing down impulse lines on a steam flow DP transmitter? Why is this done, and what precautions are necessary?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Why:** Steam impulse lines accumulate condensate and sediment over time, which can plug the lines or create false DP readings. Blowdown clears the lines.

**Question:**  
When is a "diaphragm seal" (remote seal) used with a pressure or DP transmitter? List three process conditions that require it and one disadvantage.

**Correct Answer:**  
A diaphragm seal is a flexible diaphragm that separates the process fluid from the transmitter's sensing element, connected by a capillary tube filled with a non-compressible fill fluid (silicone oil, glycerin, etc.).

## IUK-T2-PROC-213
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Explain the "auto-tune" feature on a smart valve positioner. What does it calibrate, and when should it be run?

**Correct Answer:**  
**What auto-tune does:**
1. **Maps the full valve stroke:** The positioner drives the valve from 0% to 100% and back, learning the travel limits, dead band, and friction profile
2. **Characterizes the actuator:** Determines the minimum and maximum actuator pressure required to move the valve
3. **Sets the feedback gain:** Adjusts the positioner's internal feedback loop gain for optimal response — fast enough to track commands accurately, stable enough to avoid oscillation
4. **Establishes the deadband/resolution:** Determines the minimum output change that produces valve movement

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Fisher FIELDVUE; Kuphaldt LIII Ch.26

## IUK-T2-PROC-223
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Describe the difference between a "reverse-acting" and "direct-acting" control valve body, and how the body action combines with the actuator action to determine the valve's fail position.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Valve body action (refers to how the plug moves relative to flow):**
- **Direct-acting body (push-down-to-close):** As the stem moves down, the plug moves toward the seat and closes the valve. Also called "flow-up" because flow tends to push the plug open.
- **Reverse-acting body (push-down-to-open):** As the stem moves down, the plug moves away from the seat and opens the valve. Also called "flow-down."

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** ISA-75.01; Kuphaldt LIII Ch.26

**Question:**  
What is "alarm rationalization" per ISA-18.2, and what six attributes must be defined for each alarm?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Alarm rationalization** is the systematic process of documenting and justifying every alarm in a process control system — ensuring each alarm has a defined purpose, setpoint, priority, and required operator response. The goal is to prevent alarm flooding and ensure operators can respond effectively.

**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What is "loop-powered" vs "bus-powered" in the context of FOUNDATION Fieldbus (FF)? How does power delivery differ from a standard 4–20 mA loop?

**Correct Answer:**  
**4–20 mA loop-powered:** Each transmitter draws its operating power from the same 4–20 mA loop that carries its signal. One transmitter per loop. Maximum current draw limited to 4 mA (the minimum signal value). Typical operating voltage: 10–30 VDC at the transmitter terminals.

**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What is the correct way to determine if a control loop should use direct or reverse controller action? Provide a systematic method.

**Correct Answer:**  
**Systematic method — trace the signal path:**

1. **Identify the process response:** Does increasing the controller output INCREASE or DECREASE the process variable?
   - Heating loop: increasing output opens steam valve → PV (temperature) increases → SAME direction
   - Cooling loop: increasing output opens cooling water valve → PV (temperature) decreases → OPPOSITE direction

2. **Controller action rule:**
   - If increasing CO → PV increases (same direction): Use **REVERSE action** (increase in PV → decrease in CO, to counteract the rise)
   - If increasing CO → PV decreases (opposite direction): Use **DIRECT action** (increase in PV → increase in CO, to counteract the drop by adding more cooling)

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** Kuphaldt LIII Ch.28

---

## IUK-T2-PROC-243
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** PROC  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What are "compensating measures" in the context of SIS bypass management per IEC 61511, and give three examples?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Compensating measures** are temporary risk reduction actions implemented when a Safety Instrumented Function (SIF) is bypassed, impaired, or not available — to maintain an acceptable level of process safety during the outage.

They are required whenever the risk reduction normally provided by the SIF is absent, to ensure that the overall risk does not exceed an unacceptable level.

- [not specified in source]

**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What is the difference between a SIL (Safety Integrity Level) and a Safety Function? Can you have a Safety Function without a SIL?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Safety Function:**
A Safety Function (SF) is a function to be implemented by a safety instrumented system (SIS) that achieves or maintains a safe state for the process in respect of a specific hazardous event. In simpler terms: a specific protective action the SIS takes in response to a specific hazardous condition.

Example: "Trip the main reactor feed pump and close the feed isolation valve when high-high reactor temperature (TAH-101) is confirmed — Safety Function SF-001."

**Question:**  
What is NAMUR NE 107 (previously NE 43 extension)? How does it extend NE 43's 4–20 mA fault indication concepts?

**Correct Answer:**  
**NAMUR NE 43 (background):**
NE 43 standardizes the use of fault-indicating current levels outside the 4–20 mA signal range:
- <3.6 mA: Fault (failure, wire break)
- 3.6–4 mA: Maintenance required / under-range warning
- 20–20.5 mA: Warning / over-range
- >21 mA: Failure (sensor or electronics)

## IUK-T2-STD-129
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** STD  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What is the difference between a "validated" and a "verified" SIS as defined by IEC 61511? At what stage of the safety lifecycle does each occur?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Verification:**
Verification is the process of confirming that the output of a given phase of the safety lifecycle meets the requirements set by the input to that phase. It is performed at the END of each lifecycle phase to confirm "did we build it right?"

- Each lifecycle phase (design, implementation, installation) produces deliverables that are checked against the requirements of the preceding phase
- Verification is typically performed by the organization that designed or built the SIS, though independent review is recommended
- Example: "Does the design specification meet the safety requirements specification?" — a design verification

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** IEC 61511-1 Clause 11 (verification) and Clause 12 (validation); ISA-84

**Tier:** T2 · Engineer

**Question:**  
Per ISA-18.2, what are the four basic alarm states, and what is the difference between "shelved" and "suppressed" alarm states?

**Correct Answer:**  
**Four basic alarm states (per ISA-18.2):**
1. **Normal (clear):** Process variable is within normal limits; alarm condition does not exist
2. **Unacknowledged:** Alarm condition exists but operator has not yet acknowledged it
3. **Acknowledged:** Alarm condition exists and operator has acknowledged it
4. **Return to Normal (RTN) Unacknowledged:** Alarm condition has cleared but operator has not acknowledged the return (in systems that require RTN acknowledgment)

## IUK-T2-STD-163
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** STD  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Per IEC 60079-10, what factors determine whether a location is classified as Zone 0, Zone 1, or Zone 2 for gas atmospheres?

**Correct Answer:**  
The zone classification is based on the **frequency and duration** of the presence of an explosive gas atmosphere:

- **Zone 0:** Area where an explosive gas atmosphere is **continuously present or present for long periods** (>1000 hours/year). Example: inside a fuel tank, inside a process vessel containing volatile liquid.
- **Zone 1:** Area where an explosive gas atmosphere is **likely to occur in normal operation occasionally** (10–1000 hours/year). Example: area near a pump seal on a volatile liquid, area around sample points.
- **Zone 2:** Area where an explosive gas atmosphere is **not likely to occur in normal operation, and if it does, will only persist for a short period** (<10 hours/year). Example: area around a flanged joint that might leak, area surrounding a Zone 1 area.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** IEC 60079-10-1; Kuphaldt LIII Ch.20

---

## IUK-T2-STD-169
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** STD  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
What are the ISA-84.00.01 / IEC 61511 requirements for SIS proof testing? Name three specific requirements.

**Correct Answer:**  
1. **Proof test interval must be defined in the Safety Requirements Specification (SRS):** The interval is derived from the PFD calculation and is a required input to achieving the target SIL. It is not arbitrary — it must be justified by quantitative analysis.

2. **Proof test must achieve the specified diagnostic coverage:** The test procedure must verify the full SIF function from sensor through logic solver to final element (end-to-end). Partial testing (e.g., testing only the logic solver but not the valve) provides less than 100% proof test coverage and must be accounted for in the PFD calculation.

3. **Proof test results must be documented:** All test results, as-found conditions, any deviations, and corrective actions must be recorded. This documentation is required for ongoing functional safety assessment and regulatory compliance.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** IEC 61511; ISA-84.00.01

## IUK-T2-STD-194
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** STD  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Per ISA-5.1, what is the difference between a solid signal line, a dashed signal line, and a double-dash signal line on a P&ID? Give one example device that would use each.

**Correct Answer:**  
- **Solid line (continuous):** Electrical signal (4–20 mA, discrete, thermocouple wire). Example: Connection from a pressure transmitter (PT) to a DCS AI card.
- **Dashed line (dashes):** Pneumatic signal (3–15 PSI). Example: Connection from an I/P transducer to a control valve actuator.
- **Dash-dot-dash (capillary/hydraulic):** Filled system (capillary tube from a remote seal to a transmitter). Example: Diaphragm seal system.
- **Double-dash or triple-dash (undefined/software):** Internal software link within the DCS — no physical wiring. Example: Cascade setpoint from a primary PID to a secondary PID, both in the same DCS.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** ISA-5.1 (latest edition)

## IUK-T2-STD-207
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** STD  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Per ISA-75.01, what is the critical pressure ratio (xT) for a control valve and why is it important for gas/steam sizing?

**Correct Answer:**  
**xT (critical pressure drop ratio)** is the pressure drop ratio (ΔP/P₁) at which the flow through a valve becomes choked — further increases in ΔP produce no additional flow increase. At this point, the velocity at the vena contracta reaches sonic velocity.

xT is specific to each valve type and trim design:
- Globe valves: xT typically 0.65–0.75
- Ball valves: xT typically 0.40–0.55
- Butterfly valves: xT typically 0.30–0.50

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** ISA-75.01; Kuphaldt LIII Ch.26

---

## IUK-T2-STD-215
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** STD  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Per ISA-84.00.01, what is the maximum time period allowed between safety system proof tests for each SIL level? Or is the proof test interval determined differently?

**Correct Answer:**  
**ISA-84.00.01 does NOT specify maximum proof test intervals by SIL level.** This is a common misconception.

The proof test interval (TI) is determined by the **PFDavg calculation** specific to each Safety Instrumented Function (SIF). The TI is an INPUT to the PFD calculation, and the designer selects a TI that, combined with the hardware architecture, diagnostic coverage, and common cause factors, achieves the required SIL target.

For example:
- A SIL 2 SIF with 1oo1 architecture might require a 12-month proof test interval
- A SIL 2 SIF with 1oo2 architecture might achieve the target with a 24-month interval
- A SIL 3 SIF with 2oo3 architecture and high diagnostics might achieve the target with a 12-month interval

The interval depends on: hardware failure rates (λ_DU), voting architecture, diagnostic coverage, common cause beta factor, and the target PFD range for the required SIL.

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** ISA-84.00.01; IEC 61511

## IUK-T2-STD-241
**Tier:** T2 · Engineer  
**Type:** STD  
**Weight:** 1.5×  
**Safety Gate:** NO  
**Adversarial:** NO  
**Source:** IUK_v3_IUK_v3_T2_applied  
**Format:** full_iuk  
**Review status:** source_verified  

**Question:**  
Per ISA-5.1, what do the suffix letters "A," "B," "C," and "D" mean when appended to an instrument tag number (e.g., TT-101A, TT-101B)?

**Correct Answer:**  
Suffix letters A, B, C, D indicate **multiple instances of the same functional instrument within the same loop.** They differentiate redundant or multiple instruments measuring the same variable at the same location.

Examples:
- **TT-101A, TT-101B, TT-101C:** Three temperature transmitters in loop 101 — likely a 2oo3 voting arrangement for a safety function or a redundant measurement
- **PSV-200A, PSV-200B:** Two pressure safety valves on the same vessel — parallel installation for capacity or maintenance

The suffix does NOT indicate:
- Different locations (that would be different loop numbers)
- Different process variables (that would be different first letters)
- Sequence of installation (it's not "first installed, second installed")

**Required Elements:**
- [not specified in source]

**Common Wrong Answers:**
- [DRAFT — SME review required]

**Reference:** ISA-5.1
